      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Las Vegas Valley
       </b>
       is a major
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Nevada" title="Southern Nevada">
        southern part
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
        U.S. state
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">
        Nevada
       </a>
       . The state's largest urban agglomeration, it is the heart of the
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas%E2%80%93Paradise,_NV_MSA" title="Las Vegas–Paradise, NV MSA">
        Las Vegas–Paradise-Henderson, NV MSA
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Valley is largely defined by the
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley_(landform)" title="Las Vegas Valley (landform)">
        Las Vegas Valley
       </a>
       landform, a 600 sq mi (1,600 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       )
       <a href="/wiki/Depression_(geology)" title="Depression (geology)">
        basin
       </a>
       area surrounded by mountains to the north, south, east and west of the metropolitan area. The Valley is home to the three largest incorporated cities in Nevada:
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">
        Las Vegas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Henderson,_Nevada" title="Henderson, Nevada">
        Henderson
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/North_Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="North Las Vegas, Nevada">
        North Las Vegas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Five unincorporated towns governed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Clark_County,_Nevada" title="Clark County, Nevada">
        Clark County
       </a>
       government are part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Township" title="Las Vegas Township">
        Las Vegas Township
       </a>
       and constitute the largest community in the state of Nevada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clark_County_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Clark_County-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The names
       <b>
        Las Vegas
       </b>
       and
       <b>
        Vegas
       </b>
       are interchangeably used to indicate the Valley,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Strip" title="The Strip">
        the Strip
       </a>
       , and the city, and as a brand by the
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Convention_and_Visitors_Authority" title="Las Vegas Convention and Visitors Authority">
        Las Vegas Convention and Visitors Authority
       </a>
       to denominate the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Valley is affectionately known as the "ninth island" by
       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
        Hawaii
       </a>
       natives and Las Vegans alike, in part due to the large number of people originally from Hawaii who live in and regularly travel to Las Vegas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the 1990s the Las Vegas Valley has seen exponential growth, more than doubling its population of 741,459 in 1990 to more than 2 million estimated in 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Las Vegas Valley remains one of the fastest growing metropolitan areas in the United States, and in its relatively short history has established a diverse presence in international business, commerce, urban development and entertainment, as well as one of the most iconic and most visited tourist destinations in the world. In 2014, a record breaking 41 million visited the Las Vegas area, producing a
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_metropolitan_product" title="Gross metropolitan product">
        gross metropolitan product
       </a>
       of more than $100 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Las_Vegas_Valley" title="History of the Las Vegas Valley">
        History of the Las Vegas Valley
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first reported non-
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        Native American
       </a>
       visitor to the Las Vegas Valley was the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_people" title="Mexican people">
        Mexican
       </a>
       scout
       <a href="/wiki/Raphael_Rivera" title="Raphael Rivera">
        Rafael Rivera
       </a>
       in 1829.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Las Vegas was named by Mexicans in the
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Armijo" title="Antonio Armijo">
        Antonio Armijo
       </a>
       party,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clark_County_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Clark_County-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including Rivera, who used the water in the area while heading north and west along the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish_Trail_(trade_route)" title="Old Spanish Trail (trade route)">
        Old Spanish Trail
       </a>
       from Texas. In the 19th century, areas of the valley contained
       <a href="/wiki/Artesian_aquifer" title="Artesian aquifer">
        artesian
       </a>
       wells that supported extensive green areas, or
       <a href="/wiki/Meadow" title="Meadow">
        meadows
       </a>
       , hence the name
       <i>
        Las Vegas
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        vegas
       </i>
       being Spanish for "meadows").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The area was previously settled by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon" title="Mormon">
        Mormon
       </a>
       farmers in 1854 and later became the site of a
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">
        United States Army
       </a>
       fort in 1864, beginning a long relationship between southern Nevada and the U.S. military. Since the 1930s, Las Vegas has generally been identified as a
       <a href="/wiki/Gambling" title="Gambling">
        gaming
       </a>
       center as well as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resort_destination" title="Resort destination">
        resort destination
       </a>
       , primarily targeting adults.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Nellis_Air_Force_Base" title="Nellis Air Force Base">
        Nellis Air Force Base
       </a>
       is located in the northeast corner of the valley. The ranges that the Nellis pilots use and various other land areas used by various federal agencies, limit growth of the valley in terms of geographic area.
      </p>
      <p>
       Businessman
       <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">
        Howard Hughes
       </a>
       arrived in the late 1960s and purchased many casino hotels, as well as television and radio stations in the area. Legitimate corporations began to purchase casino hotels as well, and
       <a href="/wiki/American_Mafia" title="American Mafia">
        the mob
       </a>
       was run out by the federal government over the next several years. The constant stream of tourist dollars from the hotels and casinos was augmented by a new source of federal money from the establishment of what is now
       <a href="/wiki/Nellis_Air_Force_Base" title="Nellis Air Force Base">
        Nellis Air Force Base
       </a>
       . The influx of military personnel and casino job-hunters helped start a land building boom which is now leveling off.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Las Vegas area remains one of the world's top entertainment destinations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Boundaries">
        Boundaries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Boundaries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lasvegasmetro.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="361" data-file-width="422" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lasvegasmetro.png/220px-Lasvegasmetro.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lasvegasmetro.png/330px-Lasvegasmetro.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/Lasvegasmetro.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lasvegasmetro.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cities and communities of the Las Vegas valley
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The valley is contained in the Las Vegas Valley landform. This includes the cities of Las Vegas, North Las Vegas, and Henderson, and the unincorporated towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Summerlin_South,_Nevada" title="Summerlin South, Nevada">
        Summerlin South
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paradise,_Nevada" title="Paradise, Nevada">
        Paradise
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spring_Valley,_Nevada" title="Spring Valley, Nevada">
        Spring Valley
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sunrise_Manor,_Nevada" title="Sunrise Manor, Nevada">
        Sunrise Manor
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Enterprise,_Nevada" title="Enterprise, Nevada">
        Enterprise
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Winchester,_Nevada" title="Winchester, Nevada">
        Winchester
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Whitney,_Nevada" title="Whitney, Nevada">
        Whitney
       </a>
       . The valley is technically located within the larger metropolitan area, as the metropolitan area covers all of Clark County including parts that do not fall within the valley.
      </p>
      <p>
       The government of Clark County has an "Urban Planning Area" of Las Vegas. This definition is a roughly rectangular area, about 20 mi (32 km) from east to west and 30 miles (48 km) from north to south. Notable exclusions from the "Urban Planning Area" include
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Rock_Canyon_National_Conservation_Area" title="Red Rock Canyon National Conservation Area">
        Red Rock
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Diamond,_Nevada" title="Blue Diamond, Nevada">
        Blue Diamond
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Charleston" title="Mount Charleston">
        Mount Charleston
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Metropolitan_Police_Department" title="Las Vegas Metropolitan Police Department">
        Las Vegas Metropolitan Police Department
       </a>
       is the largest police department in the valley and the state and exercises jurisdiction in the entire county. There are approximately 3,000 police officers that cover the city of Las Vegas; unincorporated areas; the town of Laughlin, about 90 mi (140 km) from
       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Las_Vegas" title="Downtown Las Vegas">
        Downtown Las Vegas
       </a>
       ; and desert, park, and mountain areas within Clark County. The department does not exercise primary jurisdiction in areas with separate police forces such as North Las Vegas, Henderson, Boulder City, Nellis Air Force Base and the Paiute reservation.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_environment">
        Geography and environment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography and environment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lasvegas.terra.1500pix.jpg">

          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lasvegas.terra.1500pix.jpg" title="Enlarge">

         <a href="/wiki/Terra_(satellite)" title="Terra (satellite)">

         </a>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Las_Vegas_at_Night.JPG">

      <p>
       The Las Vegas Valley lies in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">
        Mojave Desert
       </a>
       . The surrounding land is
       <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">
        desert
       </a>
       with mountains in the distance.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Las Vegas Valley lies in a relatively high-altitude portion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">
        Mojave Desert
       </a>
       , with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" title="Subtropical climate">
        subtropical
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">
        hot-desert climate
       </a>
       . The Valley generally averages less than 5 in (130 mm) of rain annually.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nws_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nws-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Daily daytime summer temperatures in July and August typically range from 100 °F (38 °C) to 110 °F (43 °C), while nights generally range from 72 °F (22 °C) to 80 °F (27 °C).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nws_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nws-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Very low humidity, however, tempers the effect of these temperatures, though
       <a href="/wiki/Dehydration" title="Dehydration">
        dehydration
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Heat_exhaustion" title="Heat exhaustion">
        heat exhaustion
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sun_stroke" title="Sun stroke">
        sun stroke
       </a>
       can occur after even a limited time outdoors in the summer. The interiors of automobiles often prove deadly to small children and pets during the summer and surfaces exposed to the sun can cause
       <a href="/wiki/Burn" title="Burn">
        first- and second-degree burns
       </a>
       to unprotected skin. July and August can also be marked by "
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Monsoon" title="North American Monsoon">
        monsoon season
       </a>
       ", when moist winds from the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">
        Gulf of California
       </a>
       soak much of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">
        Southwestern United States
       </a>
       . While not only raising humidity levels, these winds develop into dramatic desert thunderstorms that can sometimes cause
       <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood" title="Flash flood">
        flash flooding
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Winters in the Las Vegas Valley are typically chilly, but sunny. Winter highs in December and January usually range from 52 °F (11 °C) to 60 °F (16 °C), while nighttime lows range from 34 °F (1 °C) to 42 °F (6 °C).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nws_15-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-nws-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The mountains surrounding the valley are snow-covered during the winter season, but snow accumulation in the area itself is uncommon. Every few years apart, however, Las Vegas does get a measurable snowfall.
      </p>
      <p>
       Spring and fall are generally warm to hot.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fault_zones">
        Fault zones
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Fault zones">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The valley has seven known earthquake
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fault_zone" title="Fault zone">
        fault zones
       </a>
       ; Frenchman Mountain Fault; Whitney Mesa Fault; Cashman Fault; Valley View Fault; Decatur Fault; Eglington Fault; West Charleston Fault.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air_quality">
        Air quality
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Air quality">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Having part of the region in a desert basin creates issues with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_quality" title="Air quality">
        air quality
       </a>
       . From the dust the wind picks up, to the smog produced by vehicles, to the pollen in the air, the valley has several bad air days.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Pollen" title="Pollen">
        Pollen
       </a>
       can be a major issue several weeks a year, with
       <a href="/wiki/Pollen_count" title="Pollen count">
        counts
       </a>
       occasionally in the 70,000-plus range. Local governments are trying to control this by banning plants that produce the most pollen.
      </p>
      <p>
       The dust problems usually happen on very windy days, so they tend to be short and seasonal. Full-fledged dust storms are rare.
      </p>
      <p>
       Smog, on the other hand, gets worse when there is no wind to move the air out of the valley. Also, in winter it is possible for an
       <a href="/wiki/Inversion_(meteorology)" title="Inversion (meteorology)">
        inversion
       </a>
       to form in the valley.
      </p>
      <p>
       Since manufacturing is not a dominant industry of Las Vegas, and with Clark County working to control
       <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">
        air quality
       </a>
       problems, success has been shown over the years.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water">
        Water
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Water">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hoover_Dam,_Colorado_River.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Hoover_Dam%2C_Colorado_River.JPG/220px-Hoover_Dam%2C_Colorado_River.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Hoover_Dam%2C_Colorado_River.JPG/330px-Hoover_Dam%2C_Colorado_River.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Hoover_Dam%2C_Colorado_River.JPG/440px-Hoover_Dam%2C_Colorado_River.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hoover_Dam,_Colorado_River.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mead" title="Lake Mead">
          Lake Mead
         </a>
         shown behind
         <a href="/wiki/Hoover_Dam" title="Hoover Dam">
          Hoover Dam
         </a>
         on the
         <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">
          Colorado River
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The native
       <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">
        flora
       </a>
       does little to help the
       <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">
        soil
       </a>
       retain water. During the intense rains of
       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">
        monsoon
       </a>
       season or (relatively) wet months of January and February, a network of dry natural channels, called washes or
       <a href="/wiki/Arroyo_(creek)" title="Arroyo (creek)">
        arroyos
       </a>
       , carved into the valley floor allows water to flow down from the mountains and converge in the
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Wash" title="Las Vegas Wash">
        Las Vegas Wash
       </a>
       which runs through the
       <a href="/wiki/Clark_County_Wetlands_Park" title="Clark County Wetlands Park">
        Clark County Wetlands Park
       </a>
       . The wash system used to form a large natural wetlands which then flowed into the
       <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">
        Colorado River
       </a>
       , until the construction of
       <a href="/wiki/Hoover_Dam" title="Hoover Dam">
        Hoover Dam
       </a>
       on the Colorado River led to the creation of Lake Mead. Further development in the 1980s and 1990s made
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Las_Vegas" title="Lake Las Vegas">
        Lake Las Vegas
       </a>
       , which required directing the Las Vegas Wash into tunnels which run under Lake Las Vegas and into
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mead" title="Lake Mead">
        Lake Mead
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Nevada receives an allocation 300,000 acre feet (370,000,000 m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       ) of water
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dwy_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dwy-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       each year from Lake Mead, with credits for water it returns to the lake. The allocations were made with the
       <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River_Compact" title="Colorado River Compact">
        Colorado River Compact
       </a>
       when Nevada had a much smaller population and very little agriculture. The allocations were also made during a wet string of years, which overstated the available water in the entire watershed. As a result, precipitation that is below normal for a few years can significantly affect the Colorado River reservoirs. The Las Vegas area uses most of this allocation with
       <a href="/wiki/Laughlin,_Nevada" title="Laughlin, Nevada">
        Laughlin, Nevada
       </a>
       using most of the remaining allocation. In June 2007, the price of a cubic meter was 57 cents in Las Vegas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lip_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lip-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Las Vegas gets around 90 percent of its water from Lake Mead.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bar_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bar-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Early Vegas depended on the
       <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">
        aquifer
       </a>
       which fed the flowing springs supporting the meadows that gave the area its name, but the pumping of water from these caused a large drop in the water levels and ground subsidence over wide areas of the valley. Today, the aquifers are basically used to store water that is pumped from the lake during periods of low demand and pumped out during periods of high demand.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">
        Urbanization
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Urbanization">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The population doubling time in the greater metropolitan area was under ten years, since the early 1970s and the Las Vegas metropolitan area now has a population approaching two million people. This rapid population growth led to a significant urbanization of desert lands into industrial and commercial areas (see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suburbia" title="Suburbia">
        suburbia
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:708px;">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="">
        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg" title="Four-segment panorama of the Cosmopolitan, Bellagio, and Caesars Palace (left to right) from the Las Vegas Strip, across from the Bellagio fountains.">
          <img alt="Four-segment panorama of the Cosmopolitan, Bellagio, and Caesars Palace (left to right) from the Las Vegas Strip, across from the Bellagio fountains." data-file-height="3200" data-file-width="8000" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg/700px-Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg/1050px-Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg/1400px-Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg 2x" width="700"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bellagio_Las_Vegas_December_2013_panorama.jpg" title="File:Bellagio Las Vegas December 2013 panorama.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         Four-segment panorama of the Cosmopolitan, Bellagio, and Caesars Palace (left to right) from the Las Vegas Strip, across from the Bellagio fountains.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The driving force in Las Vegas is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourism_industry" title="Tourism industry">
        tourism industry
       </a>
       and the area has about 150,000 hotel rooms, more than any other city in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the past, casinos and celebrity shows were the two major attractions for the area. Now
       <a href="/wiki/Shopping" title="Shopping">
        shopping
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Convention_(meeting)" title="Convention (meeting)">
        conventions
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fine_dining" title="Fine dining">
        fine dining
       </a>
       , and outdoor beauty are also major forces in attracting tourist dollars.
      </p>
      <p>
       Las Vegas serves as world headquarters for the world's two largest
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
        Fortune 500
       </a>
       gaming companies,
       <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Entertainment_Corporation" title="Caesars Entertainment Corporation">
        Caesars Entertainment
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/MGM_Resorts_International" title="MGM Resorts International">
        MGM Resorts International
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNmoney_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNNmoney-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Several companies involved in the manufacture of electronic gaming machines, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Slot_machine" title="Slot machine">
        slot machines
       </a>
       , are located in the Las Vegas area. In the first decade of the 21st century, shopping and dining have become attractions of their own. Tourism marketing and promotion are handled by the
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Convention_and_Visitors_Authority" title="Las Vegas Convention and Visitors Authority">
        Las Vegas Convention and Visitors Authority
       </a>
       , a county-wide agency. Its annual Visitors Survey provides detailed information on visitor numbers, spending patterns, and resulting revenues.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Night_aerial_view,_Las_Vegas,_Nevada,_04649u.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4096" data-file-width="6144" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Night_aerial_view%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_Nevada%2C_04649u.jpg/220px-Night_aerial_view%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_Nevada%2C_04649u.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Night_aerial_view%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_Nevada%2C_04649u.jpg/330px-Night_aerial_view%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_Nevada%2C_04649u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Night_aerial_view%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_Nevada%2C_04649u.jpg/440px-Night_aerial_view%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_Nevada%2C_04649u.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Night_aerial_view,_Las_Vegas,_Nevada,_04649u.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">
          Las Vegas Strip
         </a>
         looking south at night.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Casino,_Las_Vegas_(3479650636).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="2722" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Palazzo_Casino%2C_Las_Vegas_%283479650636%29.jpg/220px-Palazzo_Casino%2C_Las_Vegas_%283479650636%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Palazzo_Casino%2C_Las_Vegas_%283479650636%29.jpg/330px-Palazzo_Casino%2C_Las_Vegas_%283479650636%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Palazzo_Casino%2C_Las_Vegas_%283479650636%29.jpg/440px-Palazzo_Casino%2C_Las_Vegas_%283479650636%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Casino,_Las_Vegas_(3479650636).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Exterior of the
         <a href="/wiki/The_Palazzo" title="The Palazzo">
          Palazzo
         </a>
         hotel. A major part of the city economy is based on tourism including gambling and ultra-luxury hotels.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       While Las Vegas has historically attracted high-stake gamblers from around the world, it is now facing tougher competition from the UK, Hong Kong and Macau (China), Eastern Europe and developing areas in the Middle East.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Las Vegas has recently enjoyed a boom in population and tourism. The urban area has grown outward so quickly that it borders
       <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="Bureau of Land Management">
        Bureau of Land Management
       </a>
       holdings along its edges. This has led to an increase in land values such that medium- and high-density development is occurring closer to the core. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Las_Vegas" title="Chinatown, Las Vegas">
        Chinatown of Las Vegas
       </a>
       was constructed in the early 1990s on Spring Mountain Road. Chinatown initially consisted of only one large shopping center complex, but the area was expanded with shopping centers that contain various Asian businesses. Over the past few years, retirees have been moving to the metro area, driving businesses that support them from housing to health care.
      </p>
      <p>
       While the cost of housing spiked up over 40% in 2004, the lack of
       <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">
        business
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">
        income taxes
       </a>
       still makes Nevada an attractive place for many companies to relocate to or expand existing operations. Being a true twenty-four-hour city,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Call_center" title="Call center">
        call centers
       </a>
       have always seemed to find Las Vegas a good place to hire workers who are accustomed to working at all hours.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Construction_industry" title="Construction industry">
        construction industry
       </a>
       accounts for a share of the economy in Las Vegas. Hotel casinos planned for the Strip can take years to build and employ thousands of workers. Developers discovered that there was demand for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-end" title="High-end">
        high-end
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Condominium" title="Condominium">
        condominiums
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 2005,
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_condominiums_in_Las_Vegas" title="List of condominiums in Las Vegas">
        more than 100 condominium buildings
       </a>
       were in various stages of development,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       however, in 2008, the construction industry went into a downturn due to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932010" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2010">
        credit crunch
       </a>
       , though the industry has since seen a rebound.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2000 more than 21,000 new homes and 26,000 resale homes were purchased. In early 2005 there were 20 residential development projects of more than 300 acres (120 ha) each underway. During that same period, Las Vegas was regarded as the fastest-growing community in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Other promising residential and office developments have begun construction around
       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Las_Vegas" title="Downtown Las Vegas">
        Downtown Las Vegas
       </a>
       . New condominium and high-rise hotel projects have changed the Las Vegas skyline dramatically in recent years. Many large high-rise projects are planned for Downtown Las Vegas, as well as the Las Vegas Strip.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">
        Construction
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Construction">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Las_Vegas" title="List of tallest buildings in Las Vegas">
        List of tallest buildings in Las Vegas
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="2784" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg/220px-Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg/330px-Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg/440px-Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vegas_Strip_from_Stratosphere.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Construction on The Strip. (2009)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Construction in Las Vegas is a major industry and quickly growing with the population. In March 2011, construction employed 40,700 people and is expected to grow with the recovering economy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the mega resorts that have defined Las Vegas today, began going up in the early 1970s, construction has played a vital role in both commercial and non commercial developments. Cranes are a constant part of the Las Vegas Skyline. At any given time there are 300 new homes being constructed in Las Vegas. Downtown and
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">
        The Strip
       </a>
       always have at least one hospitality project under construction. In addition, in recent years Las Vegas has seen a spike in high-rise housing units. Luxurious condos and penthouse suites are always being built. New suburban master planned communities are also becoming common in Las Vegas ever since
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Howard_Hughes_Corporation" title="The Howard Hughes Corporation">
        The Howard Hughes Corporation
       </a>
       began work on Summerlin, an upper-class community on the west side of the valley.
      </p>
      <p>
       The massive project
       <a href="/wiki/CityCenter" title="CityCenter">
        CityCenter
       </a>
       broke ground on June 26, 2006. Now completed at 3780 Las Vegas Boulevard South, it is the largest privately funded building complex in the world. At a cost of $9.2 billion, CityCenter was one of the largest projects in Vegas history. It put a massive strain on the construction ability and workforce of the area due to number of laborers and amount of materials required. Because of this, prices of almost any construction project in Las Vegas doubled. It is currently held by
       <a href="/wiki/MGM_Resorts_International" title="MGM Resorts International">
        MGM Resorts International
       </a>
       and has three hotels, two condo towers, and a hotel-condo building along with a large shopping and entertainment center.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">
        Housing
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Housing">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg/220px-The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg/330px-The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg/440px-The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Ridges_in_Summerlin.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Houses in the affluent
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summerlin_South" title="Summerlin South">
          Summerlin South
         </a>
         area of the valley
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Traditionally, housing consisted primarily of
       <a href="/wiki/Single-family_detached_home" title="Single-family detached home">
        single-family detached homes
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slab-on-grade_foundations" title="Slab-on-grade foundations">
        Slab-on-grade foundations
       </a>
       are the common base for residential buildings in the valley.
       <a href="/wiki/Apartment" title="Apartment">
        Apartments
       </a>
       generally were two story buildings. Until the 1990s, there were exceptions, but they were few and far between. In the 1990s,
       <a href="/wiki/Turnberry_Associates" title="Turnberry Associates">
        Turnberry Associates
       </a>
       constructed the first high rise condominium towers. Prior to this, there were only a handful of mid-rise multi-family buildings. By the mid-2000s, there was a major move into high rise condominiums towers, which affected the region's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Las_Vegas" title="List of tallest buildings in Las Vegas">
        skyline
       </a>
       around the Strip.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Las Vegas Valley is home to various suburban
       <a href="/wiki/Planned_community" title="Planned community">
        master planned communities
       </a>
       that include extensive recreational amenities such as lakes, golf courses, parks, bike paths and jogging trails.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Planned communities in the valley include Aliante, Anthem, Centennial Hills,
       <a href="/wiki/Green_Valley,_Henderson" title="Green Valley, Henderson">
        Green Valley
       </a>
       , Inspirada, The Lakes, Mountain's Edge, Peccole Ranch, Silverado Ranch, Seven Hills, Southern Highlands, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summerlin" title="Summerlin">
        Summerlin
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Technology_companies">
        Technology companies
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Technology companies">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg/220px-Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg/330px-Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg/440px-Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bigelow_Aerospace_facilities.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A full-scale mockup of Bigelow Aerospace's Space Station Alpha inside their facility in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Las_Vegas" title="North Las Vegas">
          North Las Vegas
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Some technology companies have either relocated to Las Vegas or were created there. For various reasons, Las Vegas has had a high concentration of technology companies in electronic gaming and telecommunications industries.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some current technology companies in southern Nevada include:
       <a href="/wiki/Bigelow_Aerospace" title="Bigelow Aerospace">
        Bigelow Aerospace
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petroglyph_(game_studio)" title="Petroglyph (game studio)">
        Petroglyph
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Switch_(company)" title="Switch (company)">
        Switch Communications
       </a>
       , US Support LLC, and
       <a href="/wiki/Zappos" title="Zappos">
        Zappos
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015,
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">
        Electric vehicle
       </a>
       startup
       <a href="/wiki/Faraday_Future" title="Faraday Future">
        Faraday Future
       </a>
       has chosen North Las Vegas's Apex Industrial Park for its $1 billion car factory.
      </p>
      <p>
       Companies that originally were formed in the Las Vegas region, but have since sold or relocated include
       <a href="/wiki/Westwood_Studios" title="Westwood Studios">
        Westwood Studios
       </a>
       (sold to
       <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">
        Electronic Arts
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systems_Research_%26_Development" title="Systems Research &amp; Development">
        Systems Research &amp; Development
       </a>
       (Sold to
       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
        IBM
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Yellowpages.com" title="Yellowpages.com">
        Yellowpages.com
       </a>
       (Sold to
       <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">
        BellSouth
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SBC_Communications" title="SBC Communications">
        SBC
       </a>
       ), and MPower Communications.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="623" data-file-width="600" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg/220px-Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg/330px-Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg/440px-Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_fabulous_las_vegas_sign.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The iconic
         <a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_Fabulous_Las_Vegas_sign" title="Welcome to Fabulous Las Vegas sign">
          Welcome to Fabulous Las Vegas sign
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The major attractions in the Las Vegas Valley are the hotel/casinos. These hotels generally consist of large gambling areas, theaters for live performances, shopping, bars/clubs, and several restaurants and cafes. There are clusters of large hotel/casinos located in both
       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_(Nevada_gaming_area)" title="Downtown (Nevada gaming area)">
        downtown Las Vegas
       </a>
       and on the
       <a href="/wiki/LV_Strip_(Nevada_gaming_area)" title="LV Strip (Nevada gaming area)">
        Las Vegas Strip
       </a>
       . The largest hotels are mainly located on the Strip, which is a four-mile section of Las Vegas Boulevard. These hotels provide thousands of rooms of various sizes. Fifteen of the world's 25 largest hotels by room count are on the Strip, with a total of over 62,000 rooms. There are many hotel/casinos in the city's downtown area as well, which was the original focal point of the Valley's gaming industry. Several hotel/casinos ranging from large to small are also located around the city and metro area. Many of the largest hotel, casino, and resort properties in the world are located on the Las Vegas Strip.
      </p>
      <p>
       The valley's casinos can be grouped into several locations. The largest is the Las Vegas Strip, followed by Downtown Las Vegas, and then the smaller
       <a href="/wiki/Boulder_Strip_(Nevada_gaming_area)" title="Boulder Strip (Nevada gaming area)">
        Boulder Strip
       </a>
       . There are also several one-off single standing hotel/casinos dotted around the valley and the metro area.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">
        Shopping
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Shopping">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino,_Las_Vegas.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1182" data-file-width="1776" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino%2C_Las_Vegas.jpg/220px-Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino%2C_Las_Vegas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino%2C_Las_Vegas.jpg/330px-Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino%2C_Las_Vegas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino%2C_Las_Vegas.jpg/440px-Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino%2C_Las_Vegas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shops_in_the_Bellagio_casino,_Las_Vegas.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Chanel" title="Chanel">
          Chanel
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Armani" title="Giorgio Armani">
          Giorgio Armani
         </a>
         boutiques at Via Bellagio.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Las Vegas has expanded its attractiveness to visitors by offering both affordable and high-end merchandise in many shops and shopping malls. Many hotels on the Las Vegas Strip also have adjacent shopping malls, giving the Las Vegas area the highest concentration of shopping malls in any four mile stretch of road. In addition to the malls on the Strip, there are several outlying malls in the City of Las Vegas, Henderson, and the surrounding area. The
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Monorail" title="Las Vegas Monorail">
        monorail
       </a>
       , lying somewhat east of the Strip, facilitates north–south travel, including stations at several casinos and the
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Convention_Center" title="Las Vegas Convention Center">
        Las Vegas Convention Center
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conventions">
        Conventions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Conventions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_at_CES_2014_(11891951215).jpg">
         <img alt="CES 2014 Audi TT Quattro" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Audi_at_CES_2014_%2811891951215%29.jpg/220px-Audi_at_CES_2014_%2811891951215%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Audi_at_CES_2014_%2811891951215%29.jpg/330px-Audi_at_CES_2014_%2811891951215%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Audi_at_CES_2014_%2811891951215%29.jpg/440px-Audi_at_CES_2014_%2811891951215%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_at_CES_2014_(11891951215).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">
          CES
         </a>
         2014 Audi TT Display
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Las Vegas holds many of the world's largest conventions each year, including
       <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">
        CES
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/SEMA" title="SEMA">
        SEMA
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Conexpo-Con/Agg" title="Conexpo-Con/Agg">
        Conexpo
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Convention_Center" title="Las Vegas Convention Center">
        Las Vegas Convention Center
       </a>
       is one of the largest in the world with 1,940,631 sq ft (180,290.5 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) of exhibit space. These events bring in an estimated $7.4 billion of revenue to the city each year, and host over 5 million attendees.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_shopping_attractions">
        Major shopping attractions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>

         Studio Walk at MGM Grand
        </li>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_the_arts">
        Culture and the arts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture and the arts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2195" data-file-width="3688" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg/220px-The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg/330px-The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg/440px-The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts_%26_DISCOVERY_Children%27s_Museum.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Smith Center for the Performing Arts">
          Smith Center for the Performing Arts
         </a>
         located in Downtown Las Vegas.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The "First Friday" celebration, held on the first Friday of each month, exhibits the works of local artists and musicians in an area just south of downtown. The city is home to an extensive
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Arts_District" title="Downtown Arts District">
        Downtown Arts District
       </a>
       which hosts numerous galleries, film festivals, and events.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Nevada_Zoological-Botanical_Park" title="Southern Nevada Zoological-Botanical Park">
        Southern Nevada Zoological-Botanical Park
       </a>
       , also known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Zoo" title="Las Vegas Zoo">
        Las Vegas Zoo
       </a>
       , exhibits over 150 species of animals and plants. The Zoo closed its doors in September, 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Shark Reef Aquarium at Mandalay Bay is the only aquarium that is accredited by the
       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Zoos_and_Aquariums" title="Association of Zoos and Aquariums">
        Association of Zoos and Aquariums
       </a>
       in the state of Nevada. It features over 2,000 animals and 1,200 species in 1.6 million gallons of seawater.
      </p>
      <p>
       The $485 million
       <a href="/wiki/Smith_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Smith Center for the Performing Arts">
        Smith Center for the Performing Arts
       </a>
       is located downtown in
       <a href="/wiki/Symphony_Park" title="Symphony Park">
        Symphony Park
       </a>
       . The center is appropriate for Broadway shows and other major touring attractions as well as orchestral, opera, choir, jazz, and dance performances.
      </p>
      <p>
       Bellagio Gallery of Fine Art is a facility presenting high-quality art exhibitions from major national and international museums. Past exhibits have included the works of
       <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">
        Andy Warhol
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Calder" title="Alexander Calder">
        Alexander Calder
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Carl_Faberg%C3%A9" title="Peter Carl Fabergé">
        Peter Carl Fabergé
       </a>
       . A self-guided audio tour is also offered.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Las Vegas Natural History Museum features robot dinosaurs, live fish, and more than 26 species of preserved animals. There are several "hands-on" areas where animals can be petted.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Atomic Testing Museum, affiliated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">
        Smithsonian Institution
       </a>
       , houses artifacts from the
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Test_Site" title="Nevada Test Site">
        Nevada Test Site
       </a>
       and records the dramatic history of the atomic age through a series of interactive modules, timelines, films, and actual equipment and gadgets from the site.
      </p>
      <p>
       The valley is home to numerous other art galleries, orchestras, ballets, theaters, sculptures, and museums as well.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">
        Festivals
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Festivals">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 25em; -webkit-column-width: 25em; column-width: 25em;">
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/CineVegas" title="CineVegas">
          CineVegas
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Helldorado_Days_(Las_Vegas)" title="Helldorado Days (Las Vegas)">
          Helldorado Days
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Electric_Daisy_Carnival" title="Electric Daisy Carnival">
          Electric Daisy Carnival
         </a>
        </li>

           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              g
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          While outside of the Valley, considered to be a Las Vegas destination due to close proximity.
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
      </div>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Media">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast">
        Broadcast
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Broadcast">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Las Vegas is served by 22 television and 46 radio stations. The area is also served by two NOAA Weather Radio transmitters (162.55 MHz located in Boulder City and 162.40 MHz located on
       <a href="/wiki/Potosi_Mountain_(Nevada)" title="Potosi Mountain (Nevada)">
        Mount Potosi
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Template:Las_Vegas_Radio" title="Template:Las Vegas Radio">
         Radio stations in Las Vegas
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Template:Las_Vegas_TV" title="Template:Las Vegas TV">
         Television stations in Las Vegas
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>

         </a>

          Las Vegas Weekly
         </a>
        </i>

       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summerlin_News" title="Summerlin News">
          Summerlin News
         </a>
        </i>
        and its sister
        <i>
         West Valley News
        </i>
        , serving Summerlin and Spring Valley.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Valley_Times_(North_Las_Vegas)" title="Valley Times (North Las Vegas)">
          Valley Times
         </a>
        </i>
        is a defunct newspaper that was discontinued around 1985. It covered the North Las Vegas area in the 1970s and 1980s.

          Henderson Home News
         </a>
