      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MonorailAtSahara.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/MonorailAtSahara.JPG/220px-MonorailAtSahara.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/MonorailAtSahara.JPG/330px-MonorailAtSahara.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/MonorailAtSahara.JPG/440px-MonorailAtSahara.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MonorailAtSahara.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Monorail" title="Las Vegas Monorail">
          Las Vegas Monorail
         </a>
         pulling into the
         <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">
          Sahara
         </a>
         Station in Paradise.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3,_Oct_2016.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3%2C_Oct_2016.jpg/220px-McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3%2C_Oct_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3%2C_Oct_2016.jpg/330px-McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3%2C_Oct_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3%2C_Oct_2016.jpg/440px-McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3%2C_Oct_2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McCarran_Airport_Terminal_3,_Oct_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">
          McCarran International Airport
         </a>
         Terminal 3.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2048" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG/220px-A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG/330px-A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG/440px-A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_jetBlue%27s_jet_is_taking_off_from_McCarran_Airport.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">
          JetBlue
         </a>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" title="Airbus A320">
          Airbus A320
         </a>
         taking off from McCarran International Airport.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">
        McCarran International Airport
       </a>
       (LAS) provides commercial flights into the Las Vegas Valley. The airport serves domestic, international, and cargo flights, as well as some private aircraft.
       <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">
        General aviation
       </a>
       traffic, however, will typically use the much smaller
       <a href="/wiki/North_Las_Vegas_Airport" title="North Las Vegas Airport">
        North Las Vegas Airport
       </a>
       , or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Airports_in_Clark_County,_Nevada" title="List of Airports in Clark County, Nevada">
        other airfields
       </a>
       in the county. Public transportation is provided by RTC Transit. Numerous bus routes cover Las Vegas, Henderson, North Las Vegas, and other suburban areas.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Monorail" title="Las Vegas Monorail">
        Las Vegas Monorail
       </a>
       runs from the
       <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Las_Vegas" title="MGM Grand Las Vegas">
        MGM Grand Hotel
       </a>
       at the south end of the Strip to the
       <a href="/wiki/SLS_Las_Vegas" title="SLS Las Vegas">
        SLS Las Vegas
       </a>
       at the north end of the Strip. The street
       <a href="/wiki/Numbering_scheme" title="Numbering scheme">
        numbering system
       </a>
       is divided by the following streets:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Westcliff Drive,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_95" title="US 95">
         US 95 Expressway
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Fremont_Street" title="Fremont Street">
         Fremont Street
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charleston_Boulevard" title="Charleston Boulevard">
         Charleston Boulevard
        </a>
        divide the north–south block numbers from west to east.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Boulevard" title="Las Vegas Boulevard">
         Las Vegas Boulevard
        </a>
        divides the east–west streets from the Las Vegas Strip to near the Stratosphere, then Main Street becomes the dividing line from the Stratosphere to the North Las Vegas border, after which the Goldfield Street alignment officially divides east and west.
       </li>
       <li>
        On the east side of Las Vegas, block numbers between
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charleston_Boulevard" title="Charleston Boulevard">
         Charleston Boulevard
        </a>
        and Washington Avenue are different along Nellis Boulevard, which is the eastern border of the city limits.
       </li>
       <li>
        All city street signs begin with a
        <i>
         N
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         S
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         W
        </i>
        , or
        <i>
         E
        </i>
        designation.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Until 1997, the
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desert_Wind_(passenger_train)" title="Desert Wind (passenger train)">
        Desert Wind
       </a>
       train service ran through Las Vegas using the
       <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">
        Union Pacific Railroad
       </a>
       (UP) rails that run through the city; Amtrak service to Las Vegas has since been replaced by Amtrak's Thruway Motorcoach bus service. Plans to restore Los Angeles to Las Vegas Amtrak service using a
       <a href="/wiki/Talgo" title="Talgo">
        Talgo
       </a>
       train have been discussed but no plan for a replacement has been implemented. The Las Vegas Amtrak station was located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Hotel_%26_Casino" title="Plaza Hotel &amp; Casino">
        Plaza Hotel
       </a>
       . It had the distinction of being the only train station located in a casino.
      </p>
      <p>
       Two major freeways—
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_15_(Nevada)" title="Interstate 15 (Nevada)">
        Interstate 15
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_515" title="Interstate 515">
        Interstate 515
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_95_(Nevada)" title="U.S. Route 95 (Nevada)">
        U.S. Route 95
       </a>
       —cross in downtown Las Vegas. I-15 connects Las Vegas to the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">
        Southern California
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_(California)" title="South Coast (California)">
        coastal
       </a>
       urban centers of Los Angeles and San Diego, and heads northeast to and beyond
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City,_Utah" title="Salt Lake City, Utah">
        Salt Lake City, Utah
       </a>
       . I-515 goes southeast to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henderson,_NV" title="Henderson, NV">
        Henderson
       </a>
       , beyond which
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_93_in_Nevada" title="U.S. Route 93 in Nevada">
        US 93
       </a>
       continues south of
       <a href="/wiki/Hoover_Dam" title="Hoover Dam">
        Hoover Dam
       </a>
       over the new
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_O%27Callaghan_%E2%80%93_Pat_Tillman_Memorial_Bridge" title="Mike O'Callaghan – Pat Tillman Memorial Bridge">
        Mike O'Callaghan – Pat Tillman Memorial Bridge
       </a>
       towards
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">
        Phoenix, Arizona
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Sun_Corridor" title="Arizona Sun Corridor">
        Arizona Sun Corridor
       </a>
       . US 95 connects the city to northwestern Nevada, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carson_City,_NV" title="Carson City, NV">
        Carson City
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reno,_NV" title="Reno, NV">
        Reno
       </a>
       . US 93 splits from I-15 northeast of Las Vegas and goes north through the eastern part of the state, serving
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ely,_NV" title="Ely, NV">
        Ely
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wells,_NV" title="Wells, NV">
        Wells
       </a>
       , and US 95 heads south from US 93 near Henderson through far eastern California. A three-quarters
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beltway" title="Beltway">
        beltway
       </a>
       has been built, consisting of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_215_(Nevada)" title="Interstate 215 (Nevada)">
        Interstate 215
       </a>
       on the south and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clark_County_215" title="Clark County 215">
        Clark County 215
       </a>
       on the west and north. Other radial routes include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SR_160_(NV)" title="SR 160 (NV)">
        Blue Diamond Road (SR 160)
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Pahrump,_Nevada" title="Pahrump, Nevada">
        Pahrump
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SR_147_(NV)" title="SR 147 (NV)">
        Lake Mead Boulevard (SR 147)
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mead" title="Lake Mead">
        Lake Mead
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       With the notable exceptions of
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Boulevard" title="Las Vegas Boulevard">
        Las Vegas Boulevard
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_State_Route_582" title="Nevada State Route 582">
        Boulder Highway (SR 582)
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_State_Route_599" title="Nevada State Route 599">
        Rancho Drive (SR 599)
       </a>
       , the majority of surface streets outside downtown Las Vegas are laid out along
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Land_Survey_System" title="Public Land Survey System">
        Public Land Survey System
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Section_line" title="Section line">
        section lines
       </a>
       . Many are maintained by the
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Department_of_Transportation" title="Nevada Department of Transportation">
        Nevada Department of Transportation
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/State_highway" title="State highway">
        state highways
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">
        Airports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Airports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">
         McCarran International Airport
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/North_Las_Vegas_Airport" title="North Las Vegas Airport">
         North Las Vegas Airport
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Executive_Airport" title="Henderson Executive Airport">
         Henderson Executive Airport
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>

         Ivanpah Valley Airport
        </a>
        (planned)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_bus">
        Rail and bus
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Rail and bus">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       While the Las Vegas area does not have any passenger rail service, proposals to revive passenger trains to Las Vegas have included the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desert_Xpress" title="Desert Xpress">
        Desert Xpress
       </a>
       high-speed train from
       <a href="/wiki/Victorville,_California" title="Victorville, California">
        Victorville, California
       </a>
       ; the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California-Nevada_Interstate_Maglev" title="California-Nevada Interstate Maglev">
        California-Nevada Interstate Maglev
       </a>
       , which would extend to
       <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">
        Anaheim, California
       </a>
       , with its first segment being to
       <a href="/wiki/Primm,_Nevada" title="Primm, Nevada">
        Primm, Nevada
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Railway_Express" title="Las Vegas Railway Express">
        Las Vegas Railway Express
       </a>
       ; and the
       <a href="/wiki/Z-Train" title="Z-Train">
        Z-Train
       </a>
       , which would travel six days a week between
       <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Los_Angeles)" title="Union Station (Los Angeles)">
        Los Angeles Union Station
       </a>
       and a new Z-Train Station adjacent to the Strip; and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Desert_Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Desert Lightning (page does not exist)">
        Desert Lightning
       </a>
       to Los Angeles and Phoenix. Las Vegas receives about 30
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freight_train" title="Freight train">
        freight trains
       </a>
       per day in 2004, and serves as a district crew change point, requiring all trains to stop in downtown. Freight traffic was 179,284 cars in 2004.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtcsnv_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rtcsnv-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Existing_services">
        Existing services
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

       </li>

      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">
        Roads
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Roads">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vegas_by_night_(360655015).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3828" data-file-width="2509" height="336" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Vegas_by_night_%28360655015%29.jpg/220px-Vegas_by_night_%28360655015%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Vegas_by_night_%28360655015%29.jpg/330px-Vegas_by_night_%28360655015%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Vegas_by_night_%28360655015%29.jpg/440px-Vegas_by_night_%28360655015%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vegas_by_night_(360655015).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Boulevard" title="Las Vegas Boulevard">
          Las Vegas Boulevard
         </a>
         looking south from the
         <a href="/wiki/Stratosphere_Las_Vegas" title="Stratosphere Las Vegas">
          Stratosphere
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Two major freeways—
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_15_in_Nevada" title="Interstate 15 in Nevada">
        Interstate 15
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_95_in_Nevada" title="U.S. Route 95 in Nevada">
        U.S. Route 95
       </a>
       —cross in downtown Las Vegas. I-15 connects Las Vegas to Los Angeles and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">
        San Diego
       </a>
       , and heads northeast to and beyond
       <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">
        Salt Lake City
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_515" title="Interstate 515">
        Interstate 515
       </a>
       goes southeast to
       <a href="/wiki/Henderson,_Nevada" title="Henderson, Nevada">
        Henderson
       </a>
       , beyond which
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_93_in_Nevada" title="U.S. Route 93 in Nevada">
        U.S. Route 93
       </a>
       continues past the
       <a href="/wiki/Hoover_Dam" title="Hoover Dam">
        Hoover Dam
       </a>
       towards
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">
        Phoenix, Arizona
       </a>
       . US 95 connects the city to northwestern Nevada, including
       <a href="/wiki/Carson_City,_Nevada" title="Carson City, Nevada">
        Carson City
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Reno,_Nevada" title="Reno, Nevada">
        Reno
       </a>
       . US 93 splits from I-15 northeast of Las Vegas and goes north through the eastern part of the state, serving
       <a href="/wiki/Ely,_Nevada" title="Ely, Nevada">
        Ely
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Wells,_Nevada" title="Wells, Nevada">
        Wells
       </a>
       , and US 95 heads south from US 93 near Henderson through far eastern California. A three-quarters
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beltway" title="Beltway">
        beltway
       </a>
       has been built, consisting of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_215_(Nevada)" title="Interstate 215 (Nevada)">
        Interstate 215
       </a>
       on the south and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clark_County_215" title="Clark County 215">
        Clark County 215
       </a>
       on the west and north. Other radial routes include
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_State_Route_160" title="Nevada State Route 160">
        SR 160
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Pahrump,_Nevada" title="Pahrump, Nevada">
        Pahrump
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_State_Route_147" title="Nevada State Route 147">
        SR 147
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mead" title="Lake Mead">
        Lake Mead
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       With the notable exceptions of
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Boulevard" title="Las Vegas Boulevard">
        Las Vegas Boulevard
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boulder_Highway" title="Boulder Highway">
        Boulder Highway
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonopah_Highway" title="Tonopah Highway">
        Tonopah Highway
       </a>
       (better known as the northern part of Rancho Drive), the majority of surface streets outside downtown Las Vegas are laid out along
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Land_Survey_System" title="Public Land Survey System">
        Public Land Survey System
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Section_line" title="Section line">
        section lines
       </a>
       . Many are maintained, in part, by the
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Department_of_Transportation" title="Nevada Department of Transportation">
        Nevada Department of Transportation
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/State_highway" title="State highway">
        state highways
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        East-west roads, north to south
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
         <a href="#cite_note-39">
          [38]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dt>
      </dl>

         )
        </li>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel">
        Fuel
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Fuel">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Las Vegas area is dependent on imported gasoline, diesel, and aviation fuel as is most of Nevada, which has only one refinery. The region is dependent on the
       <a href="/wiki/Calnev_Pipeline" title="Calnev Pipeline">
        Calnev Pipeline
       </a>
       as its single supply. Limited diesel is delivered to a dedicated terminal in North Las Vegas by rail. Diversified supply is dependent on the planned
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNEV_pipeline" title="UNEV pipeline">
        UNEV pipeline
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity">
        Electricity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Electricity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       About 25% of the electric power from Hoover Dam goes to Nevada,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-powerfaq_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-powerfaq-40">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and about 70% of power to Southern Nevada comes from natural gas fired power stations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nve_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nve-41">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">

      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_the_Las_Vegas_metropolitan_area" title="Sports in the Las Vegas metropolitan area">
        Sports in the Las Vegas metropolitan area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:T-mobile_Arena.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/T-mobile_Arena.jpg/200px-T-mobile_Arena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/T-mobile_Arena.jpg/300px-T-mobile_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/T-mobile_Arena.jpg/400px-T-mobile_Arena.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:T-mobile_Arena.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_Arena" title="T-Mobile Arena">
          T-Mobile Arena
         </a>
         as seen from
         <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">
          Toshiba Plaza
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Las Vegas is home to several notable minor league teams, as well as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNLV_Runnin%27_Rebels" title="UNLV Runnin' Rebels">
        UNLV Runnin' Rebels
       </a>
       , and one major professional team, the
       <a href="/wiki/Vegas_Golden_Knights" title="Vegas Golden Knights">
        Vegas Golden Knights
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NHL" title="NHL">
        NHL
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Raiders" title="Oakland Raiders">
        Las Vegas Raiders
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NFL" title="NFL">
        NFL
       </a>
       will play in Las Vegas in 2019 or 2020.
      </p>

      <p>
       Note: The Raiders will move to Las Vegas in 2019 or 2020; the Raiders franchise dates back to 1960 when it began in Oakland, and also played in Los Angeles between 1982 and 1994.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">
        Recreation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Recreation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Las Vegas has many natural outdoor recreational options.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are several multi-use trail systems within the valley operated by multiple organizations. The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=River_Mountains_Loop_Trail&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="River Mountains Loop Trail (page does not exist)">
        River Mountains Loop Trail
       </a>
       is a 35-mile-long (56 km) trail that connects the west side of the valley with Hoover Dam and Lake Mead.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Summerlin,_Nevada" title="Summerlin, Nevada">
        Summerlin
       </a>
       offers more than 150 miles of award-winning trails within the 22,500-acre (9,100 ha) community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also the 3-mile (4.8 km) Angel Park Trail, Bonanza Trail, and the county's Flamingo Arroyo Trail,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       I-215 West Beltway Trail (5 miles (8.0 km)), I-215 East Beltway Trail (4 miles (6.4 km)), Tropicana/Flamingo Washes Trail and the Western Trails Park Area Equestrian Trails (4 miles).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_Park_Landscape,_Las_Vegas,_NV.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1596" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sunset_Park_Landscape%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_NV.jpg/250px-Sunset_Park_Landscape%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_NV.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sunset_Park_Landscape%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_NV.jpg/375px-Sunset_Park_Landscape%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_NV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sunset_Park_Landscape%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_NV.jpg/500px-Sunset_Park_Landscape%2C_Las_Vegas%2C_NV.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_Park_Landscape,_Las_Vegas,_NV.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Las_Vegas" title="Sunset Park, Las Vegas">
          Sunset Park
         </a>
         at dusk
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Las Vegas Valley also hosts world class mountain biking including
       <a href="/wiki/Bootleg_Canyon_Mountain_Bike_Park" title="Bootleg Canyon Mountain Bike Park">
        Bootleg Canyon Mountain Bike Park
       </a>
       located in Boulder City which boasts itself as one of the International Mountain Biking Association's "epic rides".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary">
        Primary and secondary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Clark_County_School_District" title="Clark County School District">
        Clark County School District
       </a>
       operates all of the public primary and secondary schools in the county with the exception of a few which are contracted out to a private organization.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Selected private schools
       </dt>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Alexander_Dawson_School_at_Rainbow_Mountain" title="The Alexander Dawson School at Rainbow Mountain">
         Alexander Dawson School
        </a>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Gorman_High_School" title="Bishop Gorman High School">
         Bishop Gorman High School
        </a>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faith_Lutheran_Jr/Sr_High_School" title="Faith Lutheran Jr/Sr High School">
         Faith Lutheran Jr/Sr High School
        </a>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henderson_International_School" title="Henderson International School">
         Henderson International School
        </a>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Meadows_School" title="The Meadows School">
         The Meadows School
        </a>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Viator_School_(Las_Vegas,_Nevada)" title="St. Viator School (Las Vegas, Nevada)">
         St. Viator School
        </a>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">
        Colleges and universities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Las_Vegas_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nevada,_Las_Vegas" title="University of Nevada, Las Vegas">
        University of Nevada, Las Vegas
       </a>
       (UNLV) is in
       <a href="/wiki/Paradise,_Nevada" title="Paradise, Nevada">
        Paradise
       </a>
       , about three miles (5 km) south of the city limits and roughly two miles east of the Strip. The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nevada,_Reno" title="University of Nevada, Reno">
        University of Nevada Medical School
       </a>
       has a campus near downtown Las Vegas. Several national colleges, including the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Phoenix" title="University of Phoenix">
        University of Phoenix
       </a>
       and Le Cordon Bleu, have campuses in the Las Vegas area.
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada_State_College" title="Nevada State College">
        Nevada State College
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/National_University_(California)" title="National University (California)">
        National University
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Touro_University_Nevada" title="Touro University Nevada">
        Touro University Nevada
       </a>
       are nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Henderson,_Nevada" title="Henderson, Nevada">
        Henderson
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/College_of_Southern_Nevada" title="College of Southern Nevada">
        College of Southern Nevada
       </a>
       has campuses in Las Vegas, North Las Vegas and Henderson. Henderson also is home to DeVry University and the Keller Graduate School of Management, as well as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Nevada" title="University of Southern Nevada">
        University of Southern Nevada
       </a>
       . Other private entities in the Las Vegas Valley include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo_College" title="Apollo College">
        Apollo College
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/ITT_Technical_Institute" title="ITT Technical Institute">
        ITT Technical Institute
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Public schools
       </dt>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nevada,_Las_Vegas" title="University of Nevada, Las Vegas">
         University of Nevada, Las Vegas
        </a>
        (UNLV) is the major higher education institution in Las Vegas
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nevada,_Reno" title="University of Nevada, Reno">
         University of Nevada, Reno
        </a>
        (UNR) also has a campus for the School of Medicine in Las Vegas. The school now operates as the UNLV School of Medicine.
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/Nevada_State_College" title="Nevada State College">
         Nevada State College
        </a>
        located in Henderson, Nevada
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/College_of_Southern_Nevada" title="College of Southern Nevada">
         College of Southern Nevada
        </a>
        —formerly known as the Community College of Southern Nevada and Clark County Community College
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Private schools 4 year+
       </dt>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/Touro_University_Nevada" title="Touro University Nevada">
         Touro University Nevada
        </a>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/Roseman_University_of_Health_Sciences" title="Roseman University of Health Sciences">
         Roseman University of Health Sciences
        </a>
       </dd>
      </dl>
